Diyana as a Preventive Proof: Hanafi Treatment of Non-Muslims' Beliefs in Worldly Rulings
Analyzing how diyana affects legal consequences of prohibited acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that diyana is a preventive (dāfiʿa) proof to distinguish between obligating and repelling rulings in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Diyana repels obligations but does not create them; it is preventive, not obligating.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school treats the internal religious beliefs (diyana) of non-Muslims in worldly legal rulings (ahkam al-dunya). The core debate is whether diyana can serve as a transitive proof (hujja mutaʿaddiya) that imposes obligations on others or merely prevents the application of certain penalties. Through a detailed usul analysis, we will explore the distinction between preventive and obligating proofs, and see how this distinction resolves apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The central question: Can the religious beliefs of non-Muslims serve as a transitive proof affecting the rights and obligations of others in worldly rulings?
The objector argues that diyana cannot be transitive, citing the inheritance case of a Magian wife.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
The Hanafi school holds that diyana is a valid proof but only as a preventive (dāfiʿa), not an obligating (mūjiba) factor. The key dalil is the analogy of a father being imprisoned for his son's maintenance: it is a preventive measure, not a penalty.
Also, the practice of taking zakat from dhimmis' wine (but not pork) shows that diyana is considered, but only in a limited, non-transitive way.
3
Identify the opponent's objection and dalil
The opponent (likely a non-Hanafi or hypothetical objector) argues that diyana cannot be a proof in transitive matters, using the example of a Magian marrying his daughter: the daughter does not inherit by marriage because her diyana cannot serve as a proof against the other daughter who inherits by lineage.
This objection is applied to hadd for slander, maintenance decrees, and liability for destroying wine.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and the distinguishing principle
The Hanafi response distinguishes between preventive and obligating proofs. For example, the valuation (taqawwum) of wine remains on its original rule (because prohibition does not remove property status for non-Muslims), so liability is for the act of destruction, not for the valuation. Maintenance is a repelling obligation, akin to the father's duty.
The critical distinction: diyana is dāfiʿa (repelling/defensive), not mūjiba (obligating). Inheritance, by contrast, is a new grant (ṣilla mubtadaʾa), so diyana cannot create it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the refined answer
The practical consequence: In Hanafi law, if a non-Muslim destroys wine belonging to a dhimmi, he is liable, whereas the objector's view would deny liability. Also, a slanderer of Muslim converts who previously committed incest is still punished with hadd. The author provides a refined answer for maintenance: the spouses themselves believed in the validity of the marriage, so the judge rules accordingly due to their acceptance (taqlid), not because diyana is transitive.
This shows that diyana operates within the parties' own sphere, not as a general transitive proof.

فأما في حكم لا يحتمل التبدل فلا، حتى إنه لا يُعطى للكفر حكم الصحة بحال. ويُبتنى على هذا أنه جَعَلَ الخطاب بتحريم الخمر كأنه غير نازل في حقهم في أحكام الدنيا من التقوم، وإيجاب الضمان، وجواز البيع، وما أشبه ذلك، وكذلك الخنازير. وجَعَلَ لنكاح المحارم بينهم حكم الصحة، حتى قال: إذا وطئها بذلك، ثم أسلما كانا محصنين حتى لو قُذفا حد قاذفهما، وإذا طلبت المرأة النفقة بذلك النكاح : قُضي بها عنده، ولا يُفسخ حتى يترافعا. فإن قيل: لا خلاف أن الديانة لا تصلح حجةً متعدية، ألا يُرى أن المجوسي إذا تزوج ابنته، ثم هلك عنها وعن ابنة أخرى: أنهما ترثان الثلثين بالنسب، ولا ترثُ المنكوحةً منهما بالنكاح ؛ لأن ديانتها لا تصلح حجةً على الأخرى، فكذلك في إيجاب الحد على القاذف، واستحقاق القضاء بالنفقة، وإيجاب الضمان على متلف الخمر: وجب أن لا يُجعل حجة متعدية. قيل له: هذا تناقض؛ لأنا نجعل الديانة معتبرةً؛ لأنا نأخذ نصف العُشر من خمور أهل الذمة، والعُشرَ من خمور أهل الحرب، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله، وهذه غير متعدية، بل هي حجة عليهم، إلا أنه لا يؤخذ من الخنزير؛ لأن إمام المسلمين ليس له ولاية حماية الخنزير لنفسه، فلا يتعدى وله ولاية حماية الخمر لنفسه؛ للتخليل، فيتعدى. مسلم والترمذي بهذا اللفظ من حديث أبي هريرة. وحقيقة الجواب : أنا لا نجعل الديانة متعدية؛ لأن الخمر إذا بقيت متقومةً : لم يثبت بالديانة إلا دفع الإلزام بالدليل. فأما التقوم فباق على الأصل، وذلك شرط الضمان؛ لأن الضمان لا يجب بتقوم المتلف، لكن بإتلاف المتلف، وإذا لم يُضف إلى تقوم المحل: لم تصر متعدية. وأما النفقة : فإنما شرعت بطريق الدفع في الأصل، ألا يُرى أن الأب يُحبس بنفقة الابن الصغير، كما يحلّ دفعه إذا قصد قتله، ولا يُحبس بدينه جزاء، كما لا يُقتل قصاصاً. وإذا كان كذلك : صارت الديانة دافعةً، لا موجبة، بخلاف الميراث؛ لأنه صلة مبتدأة، لو وجب بديانتها : كانت الديانة بذلك موجبةً، لا دافعة، وإذا لم يُفسخ بمرافعة أحدهما : فقد جعلنا الديانة دافعةً أيضاً. هذا جواب قد قيل، والجواب الصحيح عندي عن فصل النفقة: أنهما لما تناكحا : فقد دانا بصحته، من بعد، بخلاف منازعة من ليس في نكاحهما ؛ لأنه لم يلتزم هذه الديانة، وأما القاضي: فإنما لزمه القضاء بالتقليد دون الخصومة، فلا تكون الخصومة ملزمة على القاضي. وأما أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : فكذلك قالا أيضاً، إلا أنهما قالا : إن تقوم الخمر، وإباحة شربها، وتقوم الخنزير وإباحته : كان حكماً ثابتاً أصلياً، فإذا قَصُرَ الدليل بالديانة : بقي على الأمر الأول.
As for a ruling that does not admit of change, then not; indeed, disbelief is never given the status of validity. And upon this is built that he (Abu Hanifa) considered the address prohibiting wine as if it had not descended concerning them in the rulings of this world regarding valuation, obligation of liability, permissibility of sale, and the like, and likewise pigs. And he considered marriage to mahram relatives among them to have the status of validity, such that he said: If he had intercourse with her thereby, then they both embrace Islam, they are muhsan, such that if they are slandered, the slanderer is hadded. And if the woman seeks maintenance through that marriage, it is ordered for her according to him, and it is not annulled until they both resort to judgment. If it is said: There is no dispute that diyana cannot serve as a transitive proof. Do you not see that if a Magian marries his daughter, then he dies leaving her and another daughter: they both inherit two-thirds by lineage, and the married one does not inherit by marriage because her diyana cannot serve as a proof against the other. So likewise in imposing the hadd on the slanderer, entitlement to the decree of maintenance, and imposing liability on the destroyer of wine: it must not be made a transitive proof. It is said to him: This is contradictory, for we consider diyana as valid; we take half-tithe from the wines of dhimmis and tithe from the wines of warring people, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. And these are not transitive, rather they are proofs against them, except that it is not taken from the pig because the Imam of the Muslims has no authority to protect the pig for itself, so it does not become transitive; and he has authority to protect wine for itself due to the possibility of making vinegar, so it becomes transitive. Muslim and al-Tirmidhi narrated with this wording from Abu Huraira. The true answer is: We do not make diyana transitive; because if wine remains valued, diyana only establishes the repelling of compulsion by evidence. As for valuation, it remains on the original rule, and that is a condition for liability; because liability is not obligated by the valuation of the destroyed object, but by causing destruction of the object. And if it is not attributed to the valuation of the locus, it does not become transitive. As for maintenance: it is legislated by way of repelling in origin. Do you not see that a father is imprisoned for maintenance of his young son, just as it is permissible to repel him if he intends to kill him; but he is not imprisoned for his debt as a penalty, just as he is not killed in retaliation. And when this is the case, diyana becomes repelling, not obligating, contrary to inheritance because it is a new grant; if it were obligated by diyana, then diyana would thereby be obligating, not repelling. And when we do not annul the marriage by resort of one of them, we have made diyana repelling as well. This is one answer that has been said, but the correct answer in my view concerning the issue of maintenance is: Since they both married each other, they both believed in its validity thereafter, unlike the dispute of one who is not in their marriage because he did not adopt this diyana. As for the judge, he is obliged to rule by virtue of his appointment (taqlid) and not by virtue of the litigation, so the litigation is not binding on the judge. As for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, they also said likewise, except that they said: The valuation of wine and the permissibility of drinking it, and the valuation of pig and its permissibility, were originally established rulings. And when the evidence for diyana becomes insufficient, it remains on the first state.
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh dispute about the legal effect of non-Muslims' religious beliefs (diyana) on worldly rulings (ahkam al-dunya). The author presents the Hanafi position that while disbelief itself is never given validity, certain acts like drinking wine or marriage to mahram are treated as valid in this world for rulings like liability, punishment for slander, and maintenance. The opponent objects that diyana cannot be a transitive proof (hujja muta'ddiya) because it would lead to inconsistencies, as seen in inheritance where the diyana of a Magian wife does not affect the inheritance of another wife. The Hanafi response distinguishes: diyana is considered as a preventive (dafi'a) rather than an obligating (mujiba) factor. For example, the valuation (taqawwum) of wine remains on its original rule, and liability is imposed because it is about effecting destruction, not about the valuation itself. Similarly, maintenance is legislated as a repelling mechanism, analogous to a father's obligation to maintain his young son. The author then provides a more specific answer regarding maintenance: the spouses themselves believed in the validity of the marriage, so the judge rules accordingly due to their acceptance, not because the diyana is transitive. The passage also notes the disagreement of al-Shafi'i regarding taking zakat from the wine of dhimmis. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree with the general position but hold that the valuation and permissibility of wine and pork were originally established rulings, and when the evidence for diyana is insufficient, they remain on that first state.

Key Terms
ديانة (diyāna): The internal religious belief or practice of a person, especially of a non-Muslim.
تقوم (taqawwum): Being considered legally valuable property subject to financial liability (ḍamān) or zakāt.
حجة متعدية (ḥujja mutaʿaddiya): A proof that has effect beyond the immediate person, affecting others' rights or obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wine is considered valuable because of the dhimmi's belief that it is permissible.
B) The destroyer is liable because the valuation (taqawwum) of wine remains on its original rule, and liability is for the act of destruction.
C) Liability is imposed because the dhimmi's diyana is a transitive proof against the destroyer.
D) There is no liability because wine is not considered property in Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
Diyana is a preventive proof that repels the application of certain prohibitions but does not create new obligations; this distinguishes Hanafi treatment of non-Muslims' beliefs in worldly rulings.

The Legal Effect of Diyanah and the Ruling on the Ignorant Rebel
Usul debate on the effect of diyanah and ruling on the ignorant rebel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the effect of diyanah (religiosity) on legal rulings and identify the Hanafi ruling on the ignorant rebel (baghi) based on usul principles.

Core Idea
Diyanah grants full immunity (isma) protecting life and property; the ignorant rebel must be debated and his corrupt interpretation rejected.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses two connected issues: the scope of a dhimmi's diyanah in establishing legal immunity, and the treatment of the ignorant rebel (baghi) who opposes clear proofs while claiming Quranic interpretation. These illustrate how usul principles like the interpretation of 'isma' and the treatment of ta'wil (interpretation) are applied to fiqh cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue regarding diyanah
Read the passage to understand the exact disagreement between Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i: does diyanah only prevent penal prosecution (Shafi'i) or does it establish full immunity (isma) that also affects financial liabilities (Hanafi)?
Focus on the example of maintenance for an imprisoned dhimmi.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof for full immunity
Examine how Abu Hanifa argues that 'isma' means preservation, and since valuation of wealth and protection of persons fall under immunity, diyanah must include both protection from prosecution and from financial liability.
Consider the author's response to al-Shafi'i's objection.
3
Examine the objection regarding usury
The text raises a potential counterexample: if diyanah grants full immunity, why do we not accept the dhimmi's permission of usury? Understand the author's rebuttal that usury is a sin in their religion, not a valid exercise of diyanah.
Compare to betrayal in trusts.
4
Understand the ruling on the ignorant rebel (baghi)
Identify the definition of a baghi: a Muslim who opposes clear proofs but claims to interpret the Quran. Note that his interpretation is considered invalid because it contradicts clear evidence.
He is treated differently from a disbeliever because he is a Muslim.
5
Apply the principle to the baghi's liability
From the passage, when a baghi destroys property or life of a just person and has no power (to resist), what ruling follows? The text is cut off, but infer the Hanafi position that he is liable and his corrupt interpretation does not excuse him.
The full ruling is that he must be debated and held accountable.

And judgment of maintenance according to the first way is invalid because of what we said. And as for this way, it is because it is of the type of payments due from the beginning, such that the need of the recipient was not stipulated. The answer of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is that the permanent need due to continuous imprisonment is not repelled by the fixed amount, so need is realized necessarily. As for al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), he made religiosity a deterrent to prosecution only, so much so that a dhimmi is not flogged for drinking wine, but other rulings are not established. The answer to him is that the valuation of wealth and protection of persons are from the category of immunity (isma), and the interpretation of immunity is preservation. So in establishing immunity through their religiosity, it is also preservation from prosecution. And we have clarified what invalidates his school, and it became clear that what we said is also in the category of defense. And it does not follow from it that they permit usury, because that is not a matter of religiosity, but rather sin in their religion. Because from the foundation of their religion is the prohibition of usury, and that is like their betrayal in what they were entrusted with in their books, because they were forbidden from that. Similarly, usury, and that is like their permitting adultery. And as for the second type: it is the ignorance of the follower of desire regarding the attributes of Allah Almighty and the rulings of the Hereafter, and the ignorance of the rebel (baghi) because he opposes the clear correct proof that has no ambiguity, so it is invalid like the first, except that he interprets (mutawwil) with the Quran, so he is below the first. But since he is among the Muslims or those who claim Islam, we must debate him and bind him, so we do not act on his corrupt interpretation. Commentary
This passage discusses two main issues. First, the effect of diyanah (religiosity) on legal rulings. Abu Hanifa holds that the religiosity of a dhimmi establishes immunity (isma) that prevents not only prosecution but also financial liability in cases like maintenance when the person is imprisoned? The text disputes al-Shafi'i's view that diyanah only prevents penal prosecution (e.g., hadd for drinking) but does not affect other rulings like financial obligations. The Hanafi view is that immunity (isma) includes protection of life and property, so it also prevents liability. The author then addresses an objection: if diyanah establishes immunity, then why do we not accept their permission of usury? The response is that they do not consider usury permissible; it is a sin in their religion. Therefore it is not a valid exercise of their diyanah. Second, the passage discusses the ignorant rebel (baghi) who opposes clear proofs but interprets the Quran. Such a person is to be debated and confronted, but his corrupt interpretation is not accepted. If he attacks a just person's property or life, and he has no power, then...

Key Terms
الديانة (al-diyanah): Religiosity or religious adherence of a non-Muslim subject (dhimmi) that grants them certain legal protections.
الباغي (al-baghi): A rebel who opposes the legitimate ruler based on a corrupt interpretation of the Quran.
العصمة (al-isma): Immunity, preservation; a legal protection that prevents prosecution and liability.

Key Takeaway
The scope of diyanah in Hanafi usul is comprehensive immunity (isma) that protects both the person and property of a dhimmi, while the ignorant rebel's corrupt interpretation does not excuse his actions.

Ignorance as a Legal Excuse: The Hanafi Principle
Explores the principle of ignorance as excuse with examples and Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that ignorance of a ruling excuses when the proof is hidden and the person is not negligent, and apply it to the cases of Dar al-Harb and newly revealed rulings.

Core Idea
Ignorance excuses only when the proof is hidden and the person is not negligent.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul lays down a foundational rule: ignorance of a legal ruling is an excuse for those who have not received the proof and are not negligent. The text explores two specific scenarios—the Muslim in Dar al-Harb who has not migrated, and the start of a new ruling—and contrasts them with the situation once the ruling becomes widespread. Understanding this principle is essential for determining liability and the validity of past actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
What is the core statement about ignorance and excuse? The passage states that ignorance is an excuse when the proof is hidden (khafi al-dalil) and the person is not negligent (ghayr muqassir).
2
List the two scenarios
Find the two examples where ignorance is clearly excused: (1) a Muslim in Dar al-Harb who hasn't migrated, and (2) a believer when a new ruling first descends and they haven't been informed yet.
The text mentions the people of Quba and the prohibition of wine as supporting examples.
3
Examine the exception
Once a ruling becomes widespread in Dar al-Islam (ishtahara wa intashara), ignorance is no longer an excuse. The person is then considered negligent for not seeking knowledge.
The analogy of tayammum without seeking water in a populated area is given.
4
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The author cites two verses: 2:143 and 5:93. Explain how these verses support the principle that past actions before receiving a ruling are acceptable, implying that ignorance is an excuse.
The footnote discusses the context of these verses; they were revealed to reassure about deceased companions.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a case where a new ruling is revealed but a person in a remote area hasn't heard about it for a week, apply the rule: the person is excused for actions contrary to the ruling during that week.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الرابع : فهو الجهل في دار الحرب من مسلم لم يهاجر : أنه يكون عذراً له في الشرائع، حتى إنها لا تلزمه؛ لأن الخطاب النازل خفي، فيصير الجهل به عذراً ؛ لأنه غير مقصر، وإنما جاء التقصير من قبل خفاء الدليل في نفسه. وكذلك الخطاب في أول ما ينزل فإن من لم يبلغه : كان معذوراً، مثل ما روينا في قصة أهل قباء)، وقصة تحريم الخمر (۲) قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَنكُمْ ﴾ البقرة / ١٤٣ . وقال تعالى: لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا طَعِمُوا (۱) قوله : مثل ما روينا في قصة أهل قباء إلى آخره: فيما تقدم [ص٥٠٠] دليل على أن التحويل لم يبلغهم إلى اليوم الثاني. وأما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جوز لهم فعلهم على ما قال الشارح: فلم أقف عليه. وأما استشهاد المصنّف بالآية فيخالفه ما رواه أبو داود والترمذي عن ابن عباس قال : لما وُجه رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الكعبة قالوا: يا رسول الله ! كيف بإخواننا الذين ماتوا وهم يصلون إلى بيت المقدس؟ فأنزل الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَنَكُمْ﴾ (۲) وأما قصة تحريم الخمر... إلى آخره فأخرج الترمذي عن البراء بن عازب قال: مات رجل من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل أن تحرم الخمر، فلما حُرمت قال رجل : كيف بأصحابنا وقد ماتوا يشربون الخمر؟! فنزلت الآية، يعني: لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا طَعِمُوا إِذَا مَا اتَّقَواْ ، وهذا أيضاً فيه ما في الأول. فأما إذا اشتهر الخطاب في دار الإسلام وانتشر : فقد تم التبليغ من صاحب الشرع ، فمَن جَهل من بعد : فإنما أُتي من قبل تقصيره، لا من قبل خفاء الدليل، فلا يُعذر. كمَن لم يطلب الماء في العمران، ولكنه تيمم والماء موجود، فصلى: لم يُجزه. وكذلك جهل الوكيل بالوكالة، وجهل المأذون بالإذن : يكون عذراً؛ لأن فيه ضَرْبَ إيجاب وإلزام، فلا بد من علمه، إلا أنه لا تُشترط فيمن يُبلّغه العدالة وإن كان فضولياً؛ لأنه ليس بإلزام محض، بل هو مخيّر . وجهل الوكيل بالعزل وجهلُ المأذون بالحجر، وجهل مولى العبد الجاني فيما يتصرف فيه وجهل الشفيع بالشفعة يكون عذراً؛ لأن الدليل خفي، وفيه إلزام ، فشَرَطَ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في الذي يُبلغه من غير رسالة العدالة، أو العدد. وكذلك جهل المرأة البكر بإنكاح الولي مثله. وكذلك قوله في تبليغ الشرائع إلى الحربي الذي أسلم في دار الحرب، ولم يهاجر إلينا، إذا لم يكن المبلغ رسول الإمام. وكذلك جهلُ الأمة المنكوحة إذا أعتقت بالإعتاق، أو بالخيار بعد
And as for the fourth category: it is ignorance in the Abode of War on the part of a Muslim who has not migrated: that it is an excuse for him in the legal obligations, such that they are not binding on him; because the revealed address is hidden, so ignorance of it becomes an excuse, since he is not negligent; rather the shortcoming came from the concealment of the proof itself. Similarly, the address when it first descends: whoever does not receive it is excused, like what we related in the story of the people of Quba and the story of the prohibition of wine. Allah the Exalted said: "And Allah would not let your faith be lost" (al-Baqarah 2:143). And He said: "There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten" (al-Ma'idah 5:93). [Footnote 1: His statement: 'like what we related in the story of the people of Quba etc.' earlier on page 500 indicates that the change [of qibla] had not reached them until the second day. As for the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted their action as the commentator said: I did not come across it. And the author's citing of the verse is contradicted by what Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Abbas: when the Messenger of Allah was directed to the Kaaba, they said: O Messenger of Allah, what about our brothers who died praying toward Jerusalem? So Allah revealed: 'And Allah would not let your faith be lost.' Footnote 2: And as for the story of the prohibition of wine... al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Bara ibn 'Azib: a man from the companions of the Prophet died before wine was prohibited; when it was prohibited, a man said: What about our companions who died drinking wine? So the verse was revealed, i.e. 'There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten if they fear Allah...' and this also has the same issue as the first.] But if the address becomes widespread in the Abode of Islam and spreads: then the notification from the Lawgiver is complete, so whoever is ignorant thereafter is only caused by his own negligence, not by concealment of the proof, so he is not excused. Like one who did not seek water in populated areas, but performed tayammum while water was present, and prayed: it is not valid. Similarly, ignorance of the agent of the agency, and ignorance of the permitted one of the permission: it is an excuse, because there is an element of obligation and binding; so knowledge is necessary, except that justice (adala) is not required in the one who informs him, even if he is a volunteer, because it is not purely binding, but he has a choice. And ignorance of the agent of the revocation, ignorance of the permitted one of the interdiction, ignorance of the master of the slave who commits an offence regarding what he disposes of, and ignorance of the preemptor of the preemption: it is an excuse, because the proof is hidden and there is obligatoriness, so Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) conditioned in the one who informs him without a message: justice or multitude. Similarly, ignorance of a virgin woman of her guardian's marriage [is the same]. Similarly, his statement regarding the transmission of laws to a warring person who embraced Islam in the Abode of War and did not migrate to us, if the transmitter is not the messenger of the Imam. Similarly, ignorance of the slave wife if she is freed, of the emancipation or of the choice after.
Source pages p. 753

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth category of ignorance that serves as a legal excuse. The ruling is that a Muslim living in Dar al-Harb who has not migrated is excused for ignorance of Islamic rulings that are hidden from him, as the proof is not accessible through no fault of his own. The same applies to a new ruling revealed by the Lawgiver: those who have not yet received it are excused, as exemplified by the people of Quba who prayed facing Jerusalem after the change of qibla until news reached them, and the companions who died before the prohibition of wine. The author cites Quranic verses indicating that their previous actions are accepted. However, the footnotes clarify that these stories are cited to show the principle, though there are alternative narrations. Once a ruling becomes widespread and known in the Muslim community, ignorance thereafter is due to personal negligence and not excused. The analogy is given of one who performs tayammum without seeking water in the city. The passage then discusses several cases where ignorance is an excuse because the proof is hidden and the matter involves obligation: the agent (wakil) unaware of his agency, the permitted slave unaware of the permission, etc. However, the person informing the ignorant party need not be just (adil) or a multitude, since the obligation is not purely binding. For cases where the proof is hidden and there is an obligation (like revocation of agency, interdiction of a slave, preemption), Abu Hanifa required the informant to be just or numerous if not via the Imam's messenger. The same applies to a virgin woman ignorant of her guardian's marriage, a new Muslim in Dar al-Harb, and a slave wife ignorant of her emancipation. The passage thus establishes a nuanced rule: ignorance is an excuse when the proof is hidden and the person is not negligent, with specific conditions for notification.

Key Terms
الجهل (al-jahl): Lack of knowledge of a legal ruling; ignorance that may or may not be excusable depending on circumstances.
عذر ('udhr): A legally valid excuse that removes liability or sin.
التبليغ (al-tabligh): The act of conveying a legal ruling to those who must follow it; notification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT an excusable case of ignorance?
A) A new Muslim in Dar al-Harb who has not migrated.
B) A person who acted before a ruling was revealed to him.
C) A person in Dar al-Islam after the ruling has become widespread.
D) An agent (wakil) who was unaware of his agency.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: ignorance excuses when the proof is hidden and the person not negligent; after widespread dissemination, ignorance is not excused.

Notification and Reliability: Abu Hanifa's Condition for Informers in Obligatory Matters
Details the Hanafi condition on the informant in cases of hidden proof and obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cases where Abu Hanifa requires the informant to be just (adil) or numerous (adad), and apply this condition to cases like preemption and revocation.

Core Idea
In cases of hidden proof that impose an obligation, the informant must be reliable; otherwise, any informant suffices.

This part of the passage refines the rule on ignorance: when the proof is hidden and the matter involves an obligation (ilzam), Abu Hanifa requires the person conveying the ruling to be just or part of a multitude. This condition does not apply to cases where the obligation is not purely binding, such as an agent's agency. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly applying the excuse in muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
From the passage, separate cases where the informant must be just/multitude (like preemption, revocation) from those where no condition is applied (like agency, permission).
Text: 'فيه إلزام فشرط أبو حنيفة ... العدالة أو العدد' vs. 'ليس بإلزام محض بل هو مخير'.
2
List the obligatory cases
The passage mentions: ignorance of the agent of the revocation, ignorance of the permitted one of the interdiction, ignorance of the master of the slave who commits an offence, ignorance of the preemptor of the preemption. Also virgin woman's marriage and new Muslim in Dar al-Harb.
These all involve an element of binding (ilzam).
3
List the non-obligatory cases
Ignorance of the agent of the agency (wakala) and ignorance of the permitted one of the permission (idhn). These are not purely binding; the person has a choice.
Text: 'لأنه ليس بإلزام محض بل هو مخير'.
4
Explain Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Since the proof is hidden and the matter imposes an obligation, the person must be certain that the news is true, hence the need for a reliable informant.
5
Apply the condition to a hypothetical
A woman is told by a single person that her guardian has married her without her knowledge. Abu Hanifa would require the informant to be just or numerous. Apply this.
The example of the virgin woman is given in the passage.

وأما القسم الرابع : فهو الجهل في دار الحرب من مسلم لم يهاجر : أنه يكون عذراً له في الشرائع، حتى إنها لا تلزمه؛ لأن الخطاب النازل خفي، فيصير الجهل به عذراً ؛ لأنه غير مقصر، وإنما جاء التقصير من قبل خفاء الدليل في نفسه. وكذلك الخطاب في أول ما ينزل فإن من لم يبلغه : كان معذوراً، مثل ما روينا في قصة أهل قباء)، وقصة تحريم الخمر (۲) قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَنكُمْ ﴾ البقرة / ١٤٣ . وقال تعالى: لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا طَعِمُوا (۱) قوله : مثل ما روينا في قصة أهل قباء إلى آخره: فيما تقدم [ص٥٠٠] دليل على أن التحويل لم يبلغهم إلى اليوم الثاني. وأما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جوز لهم فعلهم على ما قال الشارح: فلم أقف عليه. وأما استشهاد المصنّف بالآية فيخالفه ما رواه أبو داود والترمذي عن ابن عباس قال : لما وُجه رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الكعبة قالوا: يا رسول الله ! كيف بإخواننا الذين ماتوا وهم يصلون إلى بيت المقدس؟ فأنزل الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ لِيُضِيعَ إِيمَنَكُمْ﴾ (۲) وأما قصة تحريم الخمر... إلى آخره فأخرج الترمذي عن البراء بن عازب قال: مات رجل من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل أن تحرم الخمر، فلما حُرمت قال رجل : كيف بأصحابنا وقد ماتوا يشربون الخمر؟! فنزلت الآية، يعني: لَيْسَ عَلَى الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّلِحَتِ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا طَعِمُوا إِذَا مَا اتَّقَواْ ، وهذا أيضاً فيه ما في الأول. فأما إذا اشتهر الخطاب في دار الإسلام وانتشر : فقد تم التبليغ من صاحب الشرع ، فمَن جَهل من بعد : فإنما أُتي من قبل تقصيره، لا من قبل خفاء الدليل، فلا يُعذر. كمَن لم يطلب الماء في العمران، ولكنه تيمم والماء موجود، فصلى: لم يُجزه. وكذلك جهل الوكيل بالوكالة، وجهل المأذون بالإذن : يكون عذراً؛ لأن فيه ضَرْبَ إيجاب وإلزام، فلا بد من علمه، إلا أنه لا تُشترط فيمن يُبلّغه العدالة وإن كان فضولياً؛ لأنه ليس بإلزام محض، بل هو مخيّر . وجهل الوكيل بالعزل وجهلُ المأذون بالحجر، وجهل مولى العبد الجاني فيما يتصرف فيه وجهل الشفيع بالشفعة يكون عذراً؛ لأن الدليل خفي، وفيه إلزام ، فشَرَطَ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله في الذي يُبلغه من غير رسالة العدالة، أو العدد. وكذلك جهل المرأة البكر بإنكاح الولي مثله. وكذلك قوله في تبليغ الشرائع إلى الحربي الذي أسلم في دار الحرب، ولم يهاجر إلينا، إذا لم يكن المبلغ رسول الإمام. وكذلك جهلُ الأمة المنكوحة إذا أعتقت بالإعتاق، أو بالخيار بعد
And as for the fourth category: it is ignorance in the Abode of War on the part of a Muslim who has not migrated: that it is an excuse for him in the legal obligations, such that they are not binding on him; because the revealed address is hidden, so ignorance of it becomes an excuse, since he is not negligent; rather the shortcoming came from the concealment of the proof itself. Similarly, the address when it first descends: whoever does not receive it is excused, like what we related in the story of the people of Quba and the story of the prohibition of wine. Allah the Exalted said: "And Allah would not let your faith be lost" (al-Baqarah 2:143). And He said: "There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten" (al-Ma'idah 5:93). [Footnote 1: His statement: 'like what we related in the story of the people of Quba etc.' earlier on page 500 indicates that the change [of qibla] had not reached them until the second day. As for the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted their action as the commentator said: I did not come across it. And the author's citing of the verse is contradicted by what Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Abbas: when the Messenger of Allah was directed to the Kaaba, they said: O Messenger of Allah, what about our brothers who died praying toward Jerusalem? So Allah revealed: 'And Allah would not let your faith be lost.' Footnote 2: And as for the story of the prohibition of wine... al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Bara ibn 'Azib: a man from the companions of the Prophet died before wine was prohibited; when it was prohibited, a man said: What about our companions who died drinking wine? So the verse was revealed, i.e. 'There is no blame upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten if they fear Allah...' and this also has the same issue as the first.] But if the address becomes widespread in the Abode of Islam and spreads: then the notification from the Lawgiver is complete, so whoever is ignorant thereafter is only caused by his own negligence, not by concealment of the proof, so he is not excused. Like one who did not seek water in populated areas, but performed tayammum while water was present, and prayed: it is not valid. Similarly, ignorance of the agent of the agency, and ignorance of the permitted one of the permission: it is an excuse, because there is an element of obligation and binding; so knowledge is necessary, except that justice (adala) is not required in the one who informs him, even if he is a volunteer, because it is not purely binding, but he has a choice. And ignorance of the agent of the revocation, ignorance of the permitted one of the interdiction, ignorance of the master of the slave who commits an offence regarding what he disposes of, and ignorance of the preemptor of the preemption: it is an excuse, because the proof is hidden and there is obligatoriness, so Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) conditioned in the one who informs him without a message: justice or multitude. Similarly, ignorance of a virgin woman of her guardian's marriage [is the same]. Similarly, his statement regarding the transmission of laws to a warring person who embraced Islam in the Abode of War and did not migrate to us, if the transmitter is not the messenger of the Imam. Similarly, ignorance of the slave wife if she is freed, of the emancipation or of the choice after.
Source pages p. 753

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth category of ignorance that serves as a legal excuse. The ruling is that a Muslim living in Dar al-Harb who has not migrated is excused for ignorance of Islamic rulings that are hidden from him, as the proof is not accessible through no fault of his own. The same applies to a new ruling revealed by the Lawgiver: those who have not yet received it are excused, as exemplified by the people of Quba who prayed facing Jerusalem after the change of qibla until news reached them, and the companions who died before the prohibition of wine. The author cites Quranic verses indicating that their previous actions are accepted. However, the footnotes clarify that these stories are cited to show the principle, though there are alternative narrations. Once a ruling becomes widespread and known in the Muslim community, ignorance thereafter is due to personal negligence and not excused. The analogy is given of one who performs tayammum without seeking water in the city. The passage then discusses several cases where ignorance is an excuse because the proof is hidden and the matter involves obligation: the agent (wakil) unaware of his agency, the permitted slave unaware of the permission, etc. However, the person informing the ignorant party need not be just (adil) or a multitude, since the obligation is not purely binding. For cases where the proof is hidden and there is an obligation (like revocation of agency, interdiction of a slave, preemption), Abu Hanifa required the informant to be just or numerous if not via the Imam's messenger. The same applies to a virgin woman ignorant of her guardian's marriage, a new Muslim in Dar al-Harb, and a slave wife ignorant of her emancipation. The passage thus establishes a nuanced rule: ignorance is an excuse when the proof is hidden and the person is not negligent, with specific conditions for notification.

Key Terms
الجهل (al-jahl): Lack of knowledge of a legal ruling; ignorance that may or may not be excusable depending on circumstances.
عذر ('udhr): A legally valid excuse that removes liability or sin.
التبليغ (al-tabligh): The act of conveying a legal ruling to those who must follow it; notification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following cases does Abu Hanifa require the informant to be just or numerous?
A) Ignorance of the agent (wakil) of his agency.
B) Ignorance of the agent of the revocation of agency.
C) Ignorance of the permitted slave (ma'dhun) of the permission.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
In obligatory cases with hidden proof, the informant must be just or numerous; otherwise, the ignorant person is not excused.

Conditions for Accepting a Fuduli's Report in an Option
States the condition of number or justice for the report of a fuduli to be valid within a three-day option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition(s) required for the report of a fuduli to be valid according to Abu Hanifa and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Core Idea
A fuduli's report is accepted only if reported by multiple or by a single just person — but the Hanafi school splits on the need for authority.

This lesson examines a specific usul al-fiqh rule: when an unauthorized person (fuduli) communicates a rescission of a contract during an option period, what conditions must his report meet to be legally effective? The passage presents the positions of the three major Hanafi imams, highlighting how principles of evidence (number or justice) interact with contractual authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Start with the general rule: after the three-day option period, any report of rescission is invalid regardless of the reporter.
2
Isolate the fuduli scenario
If the report comes from a fuduli (unauthorized person) during the option period, a special condition applies.
The fuduli is a third party not involved in the original contract.
3
State Abu Hanifa's condition
Abu Hanifa requires either multiple transmitters (number) or a single just transmitter (justice) for the report to be valid.
The Arabic particle 'aw' indicates disjunction: either condition suffices.
4
Note Muhammad's opposition
Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees with Abu Hanifa, but his specific position is not detailed here.
This ikhtilaf reflects different assessments of the fuduli's reliability.
5
Understand Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf treats the option-holder as already authorized to rescind, so any obligation arising from the report is added to his authority.
This alternative reasoning renders the condition of number/justice less central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد الثلاث : لا يصح. وإذا بلغه فضولي : شرط فيه العدد، أو العدالة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، خلافاً لمحمد رحمه الله. فإن وُجد أحدهما صح التبليغ في الثلاث، ونفذ الفسخ، وبعد الثلاث: لا يصح، وبطل الفسخ. وأبو يوسف رحمه الله جَعَلَ صاحب خيار الشرط مسلّطاً على الفسخ من قبل صاحبه، فأضيف ما يُلزم صاحبَه إلى التزامه.
And after three [days] it is not valid. And if a non-principal (fuduli) reports to him: a condition is placed in it of number, or justice, according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Muhammad. So if one of them is found, the report is valid in the three [days], and the recession is executed, and after three it is not valid, and the recession is nullified. And Abu Yusuf made the holder of the condition of choice authorized to the recession from his companion, so whatever obligates its owner is added to his obligation.
Source pages p. 756

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of a report from an unauthorized agent (fuduli) in the context of an option to rescind a contract. The base ruling states that after three days the report is invalid. Then it discusses a scenario where a fuduli reports: Abu Hanifa requires either multiple transmitters (number) or a single just transmitter (justice) for the report to be valid within the three-day option period. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, but his exact position is not stated here. Abu Yusuf provides a different legal reasoning: he treats the person holding the option as having the authority to rescind from the outset, so any obligation arising from such a report is added to that authority. The passage exemplifies the Hanafi usul principle that the admissibility of a report depends on the reporter's credibility.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): A person who acts without authorization in a contract, but here specifically one who reports a communication regarding an option to rescind.
العدد (al-adad): Multiple reporters (at least two, as per standard Hanafi usul for reports).
العدالة (al-adalah): Justice (uprightness) of a single reporter, making his report acceptable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what condition must be met for the report of a fuduli to be valid during the three-day option period?
A) Both number and justice of transmitters.
B) Either multiple transmitters (number) or a single just transmitter (justice).
C) Only multiple transmitters are required.
D) Only a single just transmitter is required.

Key Takeaway
The admissibility of a report from an unauthorized person depends on either multiple transmitters or a single just transmitter according to Abu Hanifa, reflecting the Hanafi concern for reliability of news.

Classification of Intoxication and Its Effect on Legal Capacity
Classification of intoxication into types and statement of its legal effect on capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and prohibited intoxication in Hanafi usul and apply the ruling that permissible intoxication, like fainting, invalidates all legal acts.

Core Idea
Permissible intoxication is akin to illness, not play, so it bars the validity of divorces and transactions.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh presents a foundational classification of intoxication (sukr) based on its cause. The Hanafi school distinguishes between sukr arising from a permissible means (e.g., coercion, necessity, medicine) and that from a prohibited means (e.g., khamr). The ruling hinges on the nature of the act: if the intoxication is not due to frivolity but resembles illness, it renders the person legally incapacitated, voiding all subsequent legal acts such as divorce and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Locate the division: 'السكر نوعان: سكر بطريق مباح، وسكر بطريق محظور' (Intoxication is of two types: intoxication by a permissible means, and intoxication by a prohibited means).
The classification is based on the means (tariq), not the state itself.
2
List Examples for Permissible Intoxication
Find the examples: compulsion (ikrah), necessity (idtirar), medicinal use (banj, afyun), drinking intoxicating milk, and according to Abu Hanifa, drinks from wheat, barley, or honey.
These are cases where the intoxicant is either halal or taken under duress.
3
Note the Legal Effect
The text states: 'فإن السكر في هذه المواضع بمنزلة الإغماء' (intoxication in these cases is like fainting). Consequence: it 'يمنع من صحة الطلاق والعتاق وسائر التصرفات' (prevents the validity of divorce, manumission, and all other transactions).
This applies to all legal acts (sā'ir al-tasarrufāt), not just marriage and slavery.
4
Identify the 'Illa (Reason)
The reason given: 'لأن ذلك ليس من جنس اللهو. فصار من أقسام المرض' (because that is not from the category of play; it becomes one of the categories of illness). The lack of intentional frivolity makes it a sickness.
The illa is that the intoxication is not sought for amusement but occurs unavoidably.
5
Recognize the Implication for Prohibited Intoxication
The text begins to discuss prohibited intoxication but cuts off. From context, prohibited intoxication does not share this illa and thus does not suspend legal capacity in the same way; it may incur punishment and different rulings.
The passage ends abruptly; complete ruling is found in other sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في السكر، وهو القسم الثاني 290 السكر نوعان: سكر بطريق مباح، وسكر بطريق محظور. وأما السكر بالمباح: فمثلُ مَن أكره على شرب الخمر بالقتل، فإنه يَحِلّ له. وكذلك المضطر إذا شرب منها ما يَرُدُّ به العطش، فسكر 6 وكذلك إذا شَرِبَ دواءً، فسكرَ به مثلُ البَنْج، والأفيون، أو شَرِبَ لبناً يُسكر، فسكر به. وكذلك على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله إذا شرب شراباً يُتخذ من الحنطة أو الشعير أو العسل، فسكر منه حتى لم يُحَدَّ على قوله في ظاهر الجواب، فإن السكر في هذه المواضع بمنزلة الإغماء يمنع من صحة الطلاق والعتاق وسائر التصرفات ؛ لأن ذلك ليس من جنس اللهو. فصار من أقسام المرض. وبعض هذه الجملة مذكور فى «النوادر». وأما السكر المحظور: فهو السكر من كل شراب محرم، وكذلك السكر من النبيذ المثلث، أو نبيذ الزبيب المطبوخ المعتق؛ لأن هذا وإن كان حلالاً عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله فإنما يحل بشرط أن لا
Chapter on intoxication, and it is the second section. 290 Intoxication is of two types: intoxication by a permissible means, and intoxication by a prohibited means. As for intoxication by a permissible means: such as one who is compelled to drink wine by threat of death, then it is permissible for him. Likewise the desperate person if he drinks from it what satisfies his thirst, then he becomes intoxicated. Likewise if he drinks a medicine and becomes intoxicated by it, such as banj and opium, or he drinks milk that intoxicates, then he becomes intoxicated by it. Likewise according to Abu Hanifa, if he drinks a beverage made from wheat, barley, or honey, and becomes intoxicated from it to the extent that he is not flogged according to his view in the apparent answer, then intoxication in these cases is like fainting, preventing the validity of divorce, manumission, and all other transactions; because that is not from the category of play. So it becomes one of the categories of illness. And some of this summary is mentioned in al-Nawadir. As for prohibited intoxication: it is intoxication from every prohibited drink, and likewise intoxication from three-day-old nabidh (date wine) or cooked and aged raisin wine; because this, although permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, is only permissible on condition that...
Source pages p. 757

Commentary
This passage is a classification of intoxication (sukr) into two types based on the means: permissible and prohibited. The permissible category includes intoxication resulting from coercion (drinking wine under threat of death), necessity (to remove extreme thirst), medicinal use (banj, opium), or consumption of certain permissible drinks that happen to intoxicate (milk, or drinks made from wheat, barley, honey according to Abu Hanifa). The key legal effect is that such intoxication is treated like fainting (ighma') — it renders a person legally incapacitated, so divorces, manumissions, and other transactions are invalid. The reasoning is that this intoxication is not from the category of play or frivolity but is akin to illness. The text notes that some details are from al-Nawadir (rare transmissions). Prohibited intoxication is from explicitly forbidden drinks and certain types of nabidh (date wine or raisin wine) that are considered prohibited despite being permissible in principle. The passage cuts off, but the implication is that prohibited intoxication does not suspend legal consequences in the same way.

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): A state of intoxication that, when from permissible means, is like fainting and prevents validity of legal acts; when from prohibited means, it is sinful.
بطريق مباح (bi-tariq mubah): By a permissible means, such as compulsion, necessity, or medicinal use.
بطريق محظور (bi-tariq mahdhur): By a prohibited means, such as drinking khamr or other haram beverages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal effect of intoxication from a permissible source (e.g., drinking a beverage made from barley under coercion)?
A) Divorce is valid but manumission is not.
B) Both divorce and manumission are valid.
C) Both divorce and manumission are invalid.
D) Only transactions involving property are invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, intoxication from a permissible cause is treated as a sickness that suspends legal capacity, invalidating all legal acts.

Intoxication by Permissible Means: Definition and Legal Effect
Defines sukr mubah and its legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sukr mubah, identify its examples, and explain why the Hanafi school treats it like unconsciousness (ighma') for legal purposes.

Core Idea
Intoxication from a permissible cause is like fainting — it nullifies legal acts requiring intent.

Intoxication (sukr) is a state that can arise from either permissible or prohibited means. This passage from Usul al-Pazdawi defines the first type—sukr mubah—and establishes that it renders a person legally like one who is unconscious. We will unpack the examples given and the rationale behind this ruling, which is foundational for understanding legal capacity in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of sukr
Note that the author divides sukr into two types: permissible cause (mubah) and prohibited cause (mahzur). Focus on the first.
This classification is unique to Hanafi usul; other schools may not distinguish.
2
List the examples of sukr mubah
Read the examples: coercion under threat of death, necessity to quench thirst, medicine (henbane, opium), intoxicating milk, and Abu Hanifa's view on certain drinks from wheat, barley, or honey.
The hadd penalty is not applied in these cases.
3
Extract the legal ruling
The text states: 'sukr is like fainting; it prevents the validity of divorce, manumission, and all other legal dispositions.'
The effect is that all volitional acts are invalidated.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason given: 'because it is not a type of frivolity; thus it becomes a category of illness.'
The key is that the intoxication is not sinful or playful, so the person is excused.
5
Note the Hanafi specificity
Abu Hanifa's inclusion of wheat/barley/honey-based drinks is mentioned as his position. Some details are in al-Nawadir.
This indicates intra-madhhab differences; the relied-upon fatwa may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في السكر، وهو القسم الثاني
السكر نوعان: سكر بطريق مباح، وسكر بطريق محظور. وأما السكر بالمباح: فمثلُ مَن أكره على شرب الخمر بالقتل، فإنه يَحِلّ له.
وكذلك المضطر إذا شرب منها ما يَرُدُّ به العطش، فسكر
وكذلك إذا شَرِبَ دواءً، فسكرَ به مثلُ البَنْج، والأفيون، أو شَرِبَ لبناً يُسكر، فسكر به.
وكذلك على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله إذا شرب شراباً يُتخذ من الحنطة أو الشعير أو العسل، فسكر منه حتى لم يُحَدَّ على قوله في ظاهر الجواب، فإن السكر في هذه المواضع بمنزلة الإغماء يمنع من صحة الطلاق والعتاق وسائر التصرفات ؛ لأن ذلك ليس من جنس اللهو. فصار من أقسام المرض.
وبعض هذه الجملة مذكور فى «النوادر».
Chapter on intoxication, which is the second division. Intoxication is of two types: intoxication by a permissible means, and intoxication by a prohibited means. As for intoxication by a permissible means: like one who is coerced to drink wine under threat of death, for it is permissible for him. Likewise, the one in dire necessity who drinks from it to quench his thirst, then becomes intoxicated. Likewise, if one drinks a medicine and becomes intoxicated by it, such as banj (henbane) and opium, or drinks milk that intoxicates and becomes intoxicated by it. Likewise, according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), if one drinks a beverage made from wheat, barley, or honey, and becomes intoxicated by it to the extent that he is not hadd-punished, according to his position in the apparent answer, then intoxication in these instances is like fainting; it prevents the validity of divorce, manumission, and all other legal dispositions, because it is not a type of frivolity. Thus it becomes a category of illness. Some of these matters are mentioned in al-Nawadir.
Source pages p. 757

Commentary
This passage defines the first type of intoxication (sukr): that which results from a permissible cause. The author lists examples: coercion to drink wine under threat of death, necessity to quench thirst, medicinal substances like henbane and opium, and according to Abu Hanifa, beverages made from wheat, barley, or honey that intoxicate but do not warrant the hadd penalty. The key ruling is that such intoxication is treated like fainting (ighma'), meaning it invalidates legal acts such as divorce, manumission, and other contracts. The reasoning is that this intoxication is not from play or frivolity but rather a kind of illness. The passage also notes that some of these details are recorded in al-Nawadir (rare transmissions).

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): Intoxication, a state of loss of mental control due to substance consumption.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness or fainting; a state that nullifies legal capacity for volitional acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal effect of intoxication from a permissible cause (sukr mubah) on divorce?
A) Divorce is valid because the person is still accountable.
B) Divorce is invalid because the person is like one who is unconscious.
C) Divorce is suspended until sobriety.
D) Divorce is valid only if pronounced three times.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, intoxication arising from a permissible cause is legally equivalent to unconsciousness and invalidates all volitional legal acts.

Jest in Sales with Prior Agreement
Usul dispute on the effect of hazl in sales with prior price agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the effect of hazl in sales when there is a prior agreement, and distinguish between different scenarios using usul principles.

Core Idea
Jest in the contract is void if parties are serious; prior agreements cannot override the actual contract.

This passage presents a usul dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples over the legal effect of jest (hazl) in a sale where the parties have secretly agreed on a different price. The core issue is whether the publicly stated price or the secret agreement governs the contract. Abu Hanifa prioritizes the actual contract, treating the secret agreement as an invalid condition, while the Sahibayn hold that the secret agreement must be honored. The passage also distinguishes cases of disguise (tuljiah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The dispute concerns a sale where the parties have a prior secret agreement on the price (tawdi'ah), but in the contract they state a different price (joking). Are they bound by the secret agreement or the contract price?
The issue is whether hazl invalidates the named price.
2
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that if the parties are serious in the contract itself, the jest is void and the named price is valid. The prior agreement is treated as a condition that contradicts the contract, hence it is fasid and does not affect the sale.
The ruling applies when parties differ or agree that nothing was present.
3
State the opposing position (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that acting upon the prior agreement is obligatory, and the jested amount is void. They rely on the principle that the prior understanding should govern.
They emphasize the importance of the secret agreement.
4
Examine the Hanafi response and distinction
Abu Hanifa responds that when there is conflict between the contract (original) and the prior agreement (description), the original is preferred. The prior agreement is only a condition and cannot override the contract. However, in the case of tuljiah (disguise), both agree the sale is valid because the price is hidden but the contract is serious.
The Sahibayn distinguish between hazl in amount and tuljiah, where both agreements can be reconciled.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If parties agreed on a sale at 1000 but secretly agreed on 2000, Abu Hanifa upholds the sale at 1000 (the serious price), while the Sahibayn uphold the secret agreement, thus invalidating the sale if the secret price differs.
Practical consequence: different rulings on validity and price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن اتفقا على أنهما لم يحضرهما شيء، أو اختلفا فالهزل باطل، والتسمية صحيحة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وعندهما: العمل بالمواضعة واجب، والألف الذي هَزَلا به باطل؛ لما ذكرنا من الأصل. وأما إذا اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة : فإن الثمن ألفان عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أيضاً؛ لأنهما جدا في العقد، والعمل بالمواضعة يجعله شرطاً فاسداً، فيفسد البيع، فكان العمل بالأصل عند التعارض أولى من العمل بالوصف أعني تعارض المواضعة في البدل والمواضعة في أصل العقد ، بخلاف تلك المواضعة. وقد ذكر أبو يوسف رحمه الله في هذا الفصل في روايته فيما أعلم، كما في الفصل الأول. وأما إذا تواضعا على البيع بمائة دينار، وأن ذلك تلجئة، وإنما الثمن كذا كذا درهماً : فإن البيع جائز على كل حال ها هنا. ففرق أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله بین هذا، وبين الهزل في القدر، فقالا : لأن العمل بالمواضعتين ممكن ثمة؛ لأن البيع يصح بأحد الألفين، والهزل بالألف الأخرى شرط لا طالب له، فلا يُفسد البيع. فأما ها هنا فإن العمل بالمواضعة في العقد مع المواضعة بالهزل غير ممكن؛ لأن البيع لا يصح بغير ثمن، فصار العمل بالمواضعة في العقد أولى.
And if they agree that nothing was present to them, or they differ, then the jest is void and the naming (of the price) is valid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): acting upon the prior agreement is obligatory, and the thousand by which they jested is void, due to the principle we mentioned. As for if they agree to build upon the prior agreement: then the price is two thousand according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, also; because they were serious in the contract, and acting upon the prior agreement makes it an invalid condition, thus it invalidates the sale. So acting upon the original [principle] when there is conflict is preferable to acting upon the description, meaning the conflict between the prior agreement concerning the substitute and the prior agreement concerning the origin of the contract, contrary to that prior agreement. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in this chapter in his transmission as far as I know, as in the first chapter. And if they agreed upon the sale for one hundred dinars, and that it is a disguise (tuljiah), and the price is such and such dirhams: then the sale is valid in any case here. So Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, distinguished between this and jest in the amount, and said: because acting upon both prior agreements is possible there; because the sale is valid with one of the two thousands, and jest with the other thousand is a condition without a claimant, so it does not invalidate the sale. As for here, acting upon the prior agreement in the contract together with the prior agreement with jest is not possible, because the sale is not valid without a price, so acting upon the prior agreement in the contract is preferable.
Source pages p. 764

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the effect of hazl (jest) on a sale where the parties have a prior understanding (tawdi'ah). Abu Hanifa rules that if the parties are serious in the contract itself, the jest is void and the named price is valid, even if they had agreed on a different price privately. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the prior agreement must be honored, so the jested price is void. Abu Hanifa argues that the contract's validity is based on the parties' seriousness at the time of the contract, and the prior agreement becomes a void condition if it conflicts. For the case of tuljiah (disguise), the sale is always valid because the price is hidden but the contract is serious; the Sahibayn distinguish this from hazl in the amount, where both agreements cannot be simultaneously implemented. The passage shows the Hanafi reasoning using istihsan and preference for the actual contract over prior agreements.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joking, which in legal contexts may render a statement void if it lacks serious intent.
المواضعة (al-muwada'ah): A prior agreement or understanding between parties, often about the price, which may conflict with the terms stated in the contract.
التلجئة (al-tuljiah): A disguise or concealment of the actual price in a sale, often to protect the seller's interests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in the case where parties agree to build on the prior agreement, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling?
A) The sale is invalid because of the prior agreement.
B) The sale is valid at the price stated in the contract (two thousand).
C) The sale is valid at the price from the prior agreement.
D) The sale is void because of hazl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when there is a conflict between the actual contract and a prior secret agreement, the contract prevails because the prior agreement is only a condition that cannot override the original.

The Effect of Jest on Shuf'a Handover: Timing and Usul Rationale
Explaining the effect of jest in handing over pre-emption rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two scenarios of hazl in shuf'a and apply the corresponding Hanafi ruling, explaining the usul principle behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Jest before demand nullifies shuf'a; jest after demand is void, and the right remains.

In Hanafi usul, not all jest statements are legally ineffective. The effect of hazl depends on the nature of the right and its temporal stage. This lesson examines the ruling on jest in handing over the right of pre-emption (shuf'a), where timing is decisive. By analyzing the rationale—whether a right has become binding (lazim) or not—we uncover a subtle principle applicable to other areas of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two temporal scenarios
Read the passage and note the two distinct times: before talab al-muwathaba (immediate demand) and after talab al-muwathaba and testimony (ishhad). The key is the moment when the pre-emptor jests about surrendering his right.
Talab al-muwathaba is the first of three demands in shuf'a, required to establish the right.
2
Apply the ruling to each scenario
Before demand: jest is treated like deliberate silence—the right is nullified (tabtul al-shuf'a). After demand and testimony: the handing over is void (batil), meaning the pre-emptor retains his right.
Nullification vs. void: before demand, the right ceases to exist; after demand, the act of handing over is legally ineffective.
3
Trace the usul rationale (ta'lil)
Why the difference? Before demand, the right is weak (ghayr lazim); jest is akin to abandonment. After demand, the right becomes binding (lazim), similar to a executed contract. Thus, jest cannot annul it, only a proper rescission can.
The passage says: 'because it is of the type that is voided by option condition' – referring to khiyar al-shart, where express rejection is needed.
4
Apply the analogy to other cases
The same principle applies to 'discharge of a debtor' (ibra' al-gharim): jest in discharging a debt after it is established is void. This shows the general rule: once a right becomes binding, jest in relinquishing it is ineffective.
This confirms the usul method of qiyas (analogy) used in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تسليم الشفعة : فإن كان قبل طلب المواثبة : فإن ذلك كالسكوت مختاراً، فتبطل الشفعة، وبعد الطلب والإشهاد : التسليم باطل؛ لأنه جنس ما يبطل بخيار الشرط، وكذلك إبراء الغريم.
As for handing over pre-emption: if it was before the demand of promptness, then that is like deliberate silence, so pre-emption is nullified. After the demand and testimony, the handing over is void because it is of the type that is voided by option condition, and likewise the discharge of the debtor.
Source pages p. 768

Commentary
This passage covers the effect of jest in shuf'a (pre-emption). Shuf'a is a right that can be lost by certain actions. If the pre-emptor jests in handing over his right before making a formal demand (talab al-muwathaba), it is treated like deliberate silence and the right is nullified. However, if the jest occurs after he has formally demanded and testified, the handing over is void because it is analogous to contracts that are voidable by option conditions. The same rule applies to discharging a debtor. This shows how Hanafi fiqh classifies actions that admit of rescission (like shuf'a) versus those that do not.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption right of a co-owner to buy the other's share sold to a third party
طلب المواثبة (talab al-muwathaba): The immediate demand for pre-emption made by the pre-emptor right after hearing of the sale
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option condition in a contract, where parties have a period to rescind
إبراء (ibra'): Legal discharge or remittance of a debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the effect of jest in handing over pre-emption (shuf'a) after the demand and testimony?
A) The pre-emption right is nullified
B) The handing over is void and the pre-emption right remains
C) It is treated as deliberate silence
D) It depends on the parties' intent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the effect of jest on a right depends on whether the right has become binding (lazim) or not; timing is decisive.

The Principle of Jest in Apostasy in Hanafi Usul
A usul rule on jest in apostasy with ta'lil and distinction from duress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that jest in uttering apostasy constitutes apostasy and distinguish it from duress, applying the underlying usul reasoning.

Core Idea
Jest in apostasy is apostasy because the jester is serious in the act of jest, showing contempt for religion.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle: jest does not negate the legal effect of certain statements, particularly those that indicate apostasy. The text from Usul al-Bazdawi explains that a person who jests with words of disbelief becomes an apostate because the act of jest itself is contemptuous. Understanding this principle helps us grasp how Hanafi usul treats intent in matters of faith, and how it differs from duress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the explicit statement: 'الهزل بالردة كفر' – jest with apostasy is disbelief. This is the core rule.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text gives the reason: the jester is serious in the jest itself, free and consenting, and the jest is contempt for religion. Understand that the act itself (jest with kufr words) is treated as a manifestation of disbelief.
The jester's internal belief is irrelevant; the external act of mockery suffices.
3
Compare with duress (ikrah)
The text contrasts with the one under duress: he does not believe in what he is coerced to say, so his words may be excused. Identify the key difference: duress removes free choice and consent, whereas jest involves free choice.
This comparison sharpens the boundary of the rule.
4
Extract the usul principle
Formulate the underlying principle: in matters of apostasy, the external act of contempt undermines the claim of inability to disbelieve; intent is imputed from the act.
This relates to the larger usul principle that acts are judged by their apparent meanings (al-umur bi-maqasidiha) but here the act itself carries the meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث : فإن الهزل بالردة كفر، لا بما هَزَل به، لكن بعين الهزل؛ لأن الهازل جاد في نفس الهزل، مختار راض، والهزل بكلمة الكفر : استخفاف بالدين الحقِّ، فصار مرتداً ،بعينه، لا بما هَزَلَ به، إلا أن أثرهما سواء، بخلاف المُكرَه ؛ لأنه غير معتقد لعين ما أكره عليه، بخلاف مسألتنا هذه.
As for the third division: jest with apostasy is disbelief, not because of that with which he jested, but because of the act of jest itself; because the jester is serious in the jest itself, he is free and consenting, and jest with the word of disbelief is contempt for the true religion, so he becomes an apostate in himself, not because of that with which he jested, except that their effect is the same, unlike the one under duress because he does not believe in that which he is coerced into, contrary to our issue here.
Source pages p. 768

Commentary
This passage covers the third category: jest in apostasy (ridda). Unlike the previous categories, jest in uttering words of apostasy makes the person an actual apostate. The reasoning is that the jester is serious about the act of jest itself; he freely and willingly engages in mockery of religion, which is a form of contempt. Thus, he leaves the fold of Islam. This is distinguished from duress (ikrah), where the person does not internally believe. The effect is the same as if he had serious intent: he becomes an apostate. This illustrates that some legal acts cannot be nullified by jest because the act itself (kufr) is inherently contradictory to faith.

Key Terms
الردة (al-ridda): Apostasy from Islam by word or deed.
المكره (al-mukrah): One who is compelled under duress to say or do something.
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest, joking, or playful speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does jest in uttering apostasy make one an apostate?
A) Because the jester believes in the words he says.
B) Because the jester is serious in the act of jest and shows contempt for religion.
C) Because the words alone without intent can cause apostasy.
D) Because jest is a form of coercion.

Key Takeaway
Jest with words of apostasy is itself apostasy in Hanafi fiqh because the act of jest shows contempt, unlike duress where free will is absent.

The Effect of Jest (Hazl) in Legal Acts: A Usul Analysis
Explaining the ruling of hazl in property and acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul distinction between acts that admit rescission and those that do not, and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding hazl in transactions.

Core Idea
Jest voids acknowledgments but affects transactions differently depending on the parties' intent.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi examines how jest (hazl) impacts different legal acts. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the act and the mutual understanding of the parties. Understanding this usul principle helps clarify why some acts are voided by jest while others are not and highlights the methodological divergence between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of hazl cases
The passage discusses hazl in three distinct contexts: transactions concerning the principal amount (mal), surrender of pre-emption (shuf'a), and acknowledgment (iqrar). Each has a different ruling.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's approach based on mutual intent
For the first category, Abu Hanifa distinguishes three scenarios based on the parties' agreed intent: disregard, construction, or no intent. The ruling depends on their mutual understanding.
This reflects the usul principle that legal effects are tied to intentions (al-umur bi-maqasidiha).
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's objective approach
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the named amount is always due regardless of intent, treating the jest as analogous to a binding contract that does not admit rescission.
Their view emphasizes the literal expression over underlying intent.
4
Apply the usul distinction to pre-emption and acknowledgment
Surrender of pre-emption before demand is like silence (voiding the right); after demand it is invalid due to its revocable nature. Acknowledgment is voided entirely by hazl because it depends on truthfulness, and jest negates the reported matter.
Acknowledgment is treated like acts that are void by coercion – it cannot be ratified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك إن اختلفا. وأما إذا هَزَلا بأصل المال فذَكَرَا الدنانير تلجئةً، وغرضُهما الدراهم فإن المسمى هو الواجب عندهما في هذا بكل حال، وصار كالذي لا يحتمل الفسخ تبعاً. وأما عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله : فإن اتفقا على الإعراض: وجب المسمى، وإن اتفقا على البناء توقف الطلاق، وإن اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيء : وجب المسمى، ووقع الطلاق. : وإن اختلفا فالقول قول من يدعي الإعراض، وكذلك هذا في نظائره. وأما تسليم الشفعة : فإن كان قبل طلب المواثبة : فإن ذلك كالسكوت مختاراً، فتبطل الشفعة، وبعد الطلب والإشهاد : التسليم باطل؛ لأنه جنس ما يبطل بخيار الشرط، وكذلك إبراء الغريم. من وأما القسم الثاني، وهو الإقرار فإن الهزل يُبطله، سواء كان إقراراً بما يحتمل الفسخ، أو بما لا يحتمله ؛ لأنه يعتمد صحة المخبر به والهزل يدل على عدم المخبر به فصار ذلك كله من جنس ما يحتمل النقض، ألا يُرى أن الإقرار بالطلاق والعتاق مما يبطل بالكره أصلاً، فكذلك يبطل بالهزل بطلاناً لا يحتمل الإجازة.
And likewise if they differ. As for when they jest regarding the principal of the wealth and they mention dinars as a subterfuge while their purpose is dirhams, then the named amount is obligatory according to them (the two companions) in this case in all circumstances, and it becomes like that which does not admit of rescission indirectly. As for according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): if they agree on disregard, the named amount is obligatory; if they agree on construction, the divorce is suspended; if they agree that nothing occurred to them, the named amount is obligatory and the divorce occurs. And if they differ, the statement is that of the one who claims disregard, and likewise this in its parallels. As for the surrender of pre-emption: if it is before the immediate demand, then that is like silence willingly, so the right of pre-emption is void; after demand and witnessing, the surrender is invalid because it is of the type that is invalidated by the option of condition, and similarly the discharge of a debtor. As for the second category, which is acknowledgment, jest invalidates it, whether it is an acknowledgment of something that admits of rescission or something that does not; because it depends on the truth of the reported matter, and jest indicates the non-existence of the reported matter, so all of that becomes of the type that admits of revocation. Do you not see that acknowledgment of divorce and manumission is invalidated by coercion fundamentally, so likewise it is invalidated by jest in a manner that does not permit ratification.
Source pages p. 768

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of jest (hazl) in legal acts. The first part covers transactions involving the principal (mal) when both parties jest about the amount. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that the named amount is always due, analogous to a binding contract. Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on their intention: if they agree they were disregarding the jest, the named amount is due; if they agree they were constructing a real transaction, divorce is pending; if they had no real intent, the named amount is due and divorce occurs. If they differ, the claim of disregard is accepted. The second part addresses surrender of pre-emption (shuf'a): before demand, it is like silence and voids the right; after demand and formal testimony, surrender is invalid because it resembles a contract with an option condition. The third part concerns acknowledgment (iqrar): hazl invalidates it entirely, whether the subject matter is revocable or not, because acknowledgment depends on truthfulness, and jest negates the truth of the reported matter. Just as acknowledgment under coercion is void, so is acknowledgment made in jest, and it cannot be ratified later.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jesting or joking in legal speech, stating something without intending its legal effect.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or obligation upon oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, can an acknowledgment made in jest be ratified later?
A) Yes, if the person confirms it later.
B) No, it is void and cannot be ratified.
C) Yes, only if it is about a revocable matter.
D) No, but it can be considered as a promise.

Key Takeaway
Jest invalidates acknowledgment absolutely but affects transactions based on the parties' intent, with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn revolving around the weight of intent vs. literal expression.
